# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubernetes Server-Side Apply Configuration Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a deep guide for applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply semantics, including conflict handling and workflow patterns.

## Scope

Focus on the applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

78-assistanttext-
The document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

---

**Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries**
Server-Side Apply is a declarative mutation model where clients submit partial intent and the server owns merging, conflict detection, and field ownership tracking via `metadata.managedFields`. The guide maps all three layers: client-side applyconfigurations, the server-side managedfields engine, and the HTTP handler entry point.

**applyconfigurations Package**
All fields as pointers is the core design decision — it allows fields to be absent from serialised YAML rather than present as zero values. The document explains exactly why the regular API types cannot be used for apply requests (a marshalled `HorizontalPodAutoscaler` with an unset `maxReplicas` emits `maxReplicas: 0`, which directs the autoscaler to scale to zero).

**Code Generator**
`applyconfiguration-gen` (`staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/`) reads API Go types plus an OpenAPI schema to produce pointer-for-all-fields structs, `With*` builder methods, and `Extract*` functions.

**The Manager Decorator Stack**
`NewDefaultFieldManager` assembles nine decorator layers (`VersionCheckManager` → `LastAppliedUpdater` → … → `structuredMergeManager`), each with a single, verifiable responsibility. The document traces every layer from `internal/fieldmanager.go:57`.

**End-to-End Request Flow**
From `PatchResource()` in `patch.go` through `applyPatcher`, `FieldManager.Apply`, the decorator stack, `structuredMergeManager`, and the SMD library's `merge.Updater.Apply`.

**Conflict Handling**
How `merge.Conflicts` becomes an HTTP 409 via `NewConflictError`, and the four resolution strategies (force, omit, different manager name, extract-modify-apply).


... (truncated)

This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\\n141: blocking the informer's watch stream.\\n142: \\n143: For high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\\n144: solution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\\n145: shared `Lease` object.\\n146: \\n147: ## Server-Side Apply\\n148: \\n149: `client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\\n150: server's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\\n151: model that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\\n152: **`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\\n153: construct the declarative patch.\\n154: \\n155: ## Versioning and Compatibility\\n156: \\n157: `client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. 36. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative mutation model in which a client submits its *intent* \u2014 a\npartial description of an object containing only the fields it cares about \u2014 and the API server\nperforms the merge, tracks field ownership via `metadata.managedFields`, and surfaces ownership\nconflicts. This differs from a `PUT` (full replacement) or a strategic-merge-patch (client-computed\ndelta) in a fundamental way: the server is the authoritative arbiter of which manager owns which\nfield, and it maintains that record across reconciliation loops.\n\nThe subsystem spans two distinct layers:\n\n| Layer | Location | Role |\n|---|---|---|\n| Client | `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Typed, partial-object builders used to construct apply requests |\n| Server | `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Field-ownership tracking and structured merge |\n| HTTP entry | `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | Routes PATCH requests with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml` into the SSA path |\n| Code generation | `staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/` | Generates the client-side builder types |\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n\n- `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` \u2014 the external library that performs the actual structural\n  merge and conflict detection. The Kubernetes code calls `merge.Updater.Apply()` and\n  `merge.Updater.Update()` from this library.\n- `k8s.io/kube-openapi` \u2014 provides `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI` which converts the OpenAPI\n  v2/v3 spec into the SMD schema format used for typed merges.\n- `k8s.io/gengo/v2` \u2014 the code generation framework used by `applyconfiguration-gen`.\n\n**Downstream consumers:**\n\n- Every typed client in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/` exposes an `Apply()`\n  method that accepts an applyConfiguration type and calls the SSA HTTP endpoint.\n- Controllers in `pkg/controller/` (e.g., `pkg/controller/clusterroleaggregation/`) use SSA for\n  all write operations to avoid the read-modify-update race condition.\n- `kubectl apply --server-side` translates user-supplied YAML into an SSA request.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Splits\n\n### 2.1 The applyconfigurations Package\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/`\n\nEvery Kubernetes API type has a parallel \"apply configuration\" type. The core property of these\ntypes is that **all fields are pointers**, so a field that is never set serialises as absent (rather\nthan as its zero value). This is the problem the package solves:\n\n```go\n// Regular struct: spec.maxReplicas marshals as 0 if omitted \u2014 wrong for an apply request.\nhpa := v1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler{Spec: v1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec{MinReplicas: ptr(0)}}\n\n// Apply configuration: omitted fields are simply absent from the YAML.\nhpaAC := v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(name, ns).\n    WithSpec(v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().WithMinReplicas(0))\n```\n\nThis distinction is not cosmetic. If `maxReplicas` is included in the serialised patch, the server\nwill interpret it as this manager claiming ownership of the `maxReplicas` field and will set it,\npossibly overriding another manager's intent. The pointer-for-all-fields design prevents accidental\nfield claiming.\n\nEach apply configuration type is named `<Type>ApplyConfiguration`. The package also exposes:\n\n- `With<FieldName>()` builder methods that accept values (not pointers), isolating callers from the\n  pointer mechanics.\n- Constructor functions like `DeploymentApplyConfiguration()` for nested structs, and\n  `Deployment(name, namespace)` for root types that pre-populate `kind` and `apiVersion`.\n- `Extract<Type>(obj, fieldManager)` functions that populate an applyConfiguration from the\n  managed-fields owned by a given manager (see \u00a74 for the extract workflow).\n\nThe top-level `utils.go` file (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/utils.go`) is\nalso generated: it provides `ForKind(gvk)` which returns a blank applyConfiguration interface{}\nindexed by GVK, useful when working dynamically.\n\n### 2.2 applyconfiguration-gen\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/`\n\nThe code generator that produces the applyconfigurations package. It operates on the API Go types\nand an OpenAPI schema file.\n\nKey files:\n\n- `generators/targets.go` \u2014 entry point; calls `packageTypesForInputs`, builds the `refGraph` and\n  `typeModels`, then invokes per-type generators.\n- `generators/applyconfiguration.go` \u2014 generates the struct type and all `With*` methods for a\n  single type. Also generates the `Extract<Type>Into` function when an OpenAPI type is available.\n- `generators/refgraph.go` \u2014 builds the reference graph of which API types reference which, to\n  determine which types need an apply configuration generated.\n- `args/args.go` \u2014 defines `ExternalApplyConfigurations`, a map that tells the generator to reuse\n  existing apply configurations for types it does not control (e.g., `metav1.Condition` maps to\n  `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1`).\n\nA type requires an apply configuration if and only if it is a struct type with JSON-tagged fields\n(`requiresApplyConfiguration` in `refgraph.go`). Top-level API types (those with ObjectMeta) get\nboth an `Apply()` client method and an `Extract()` function; embedded types get only the struct and\n`With*` builders.\n\n### 2.3 The managedfields Package\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/`\n\nThis is the server-side engine. The public surface is small:\n\n```go\n// fieldmanager.go\nfunc NewDefaultFieldManager(...) (*FieldManager, error)\nfunc NewDefaultCRDFieldManager(...) (*FieldManager, error)\n```\n\n`FieldManager` (re-exported from `internal.FieldManager`) has two methods:\n\n```go\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, manager string) (runtime.Object, error)\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, error)\n```\n\n- `Update` handles regular PUT/PATCH operations: it does not merge; it simply recomputes which\n  fields changed and updates the manager's ownership record.\n- `Apply` handles the SSA path: it merges the applied configuration into the live object.\n\nOther public files:\n\n- `extract.go` \u2014 `ExtractInto()`: reconstructs an applyConfiguration from the managed fields owned\n  by a given manager.\n- `scalehandler.go` \u2014 `ScaleHandler`: translates managed field paths between a resource and its\n  `scale` subresource (because `spec.replicas` lives at a different path in a `Scale` object vs. in\n  a `Deployment`).\n- `typeconverter.go` \u2014 `TypeConverter` interface and `NewTypeConverter()`: converts\n  `runtime.Object` to `typed.TypedValue` using the OpenAPI-derived schema.\n- `gvkparser.go` \u2014 parses GVK from a YAML file; used in tests.\n\n#### 2.3.1 The Manager Decorator Stack\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` composes a layered stack of `Manager` interface implementations. The order\nfrom outermost to innermost is:\n\n```\nVersionCheckManager                  (versioncheck.go)\n  \u2514\u2500 LastAppliedUpdater              (lastappliedupdater.go)\n       \u2514\u2500 LastAppliedManager         (lastappliedmanager.go)\n            \u2514\u2500 ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager  (skipnonapplied.go)\n                 \u2514\u2500 CapManagersManager             (capmanagers.go)\n                      \u2514\u2500 BuildManagerInfoManager   (buildmanagerinfo.go)\n                           \u2514\u2500 ManagedFieldsUpdater (managedfieldsupdater.go)\n                                \u2514\u2500 StripMetaManager (stripmeta.go)\n                                     \u2514\u2500 structuredMergeManager  (structuredmerge.go)\n```\n\nEach layer is responsible for exactly one concern:\n\n| Layer | File | Responsibility |\n|---|---|---|\n| `VersionCheckManager` | `internal/versioncheck.go` | Rejects apply requests whose GVK does not match the resource GVK |\n| `LastAppliedUpdater` | `internal/lastappliedupdater.go` | When the field manager is `\"kubectl\"` and the live object has a `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation, syncs that annotation with the new object body after a successful apply |\n| `LastAppliedManager` | `internal/lastappliedmanager.go` | On the first SSA from kubectl, migrates the annotation-based `last-applied-configuration` into managed fields |\n| `ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager` | `internal/skipnonapplied.go` | For objects with no managed fields, skips tracking on updates (lazy bootstrapping). On create, tracks managed fields with probability `DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability` (currently 1.0). On the first apply to an untracked object, bootstraps by running an `Update` with the live object under a synthetic `\"before-first-apply\"` manager before the actual apply |\n| `CapManagersManager` | `internal/capmanagers.go` | Limits update-manager entries to `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` (10) by merging the oldest entries into versioned buckets named `\"ancient-changes\"` |\n| `BuildManagerInfoManager` | `internal/buildmanagerinfo.go` | Serialises the manager name, operation type, API version, and subresource into a canonical JSON key used as the manager identifier in the internal `fieldpath.ManagedFields` map |\n| `ManagedFieldsUpdater` | `internal/managedfieldsupdater.go` | Sets the timestamp (`metav1.Time`) on the manager's entry when fields change. Uses a temporary `\"current-operation\"` manager key during `Update` to detect whether any fields actually changed |\n| `StripMetaManager` | `internal/stripmeta.go` | After the merge, removes server-managed fields (`apiVersion`, `kind`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.namespace`, `metadata.managedFields`, `metadata.resourceVersion`, etc.) from the manager's field set so they are never tracked |\n| `structuredMergeManager` | `internal/structuredmerge.go` | Converts objects to SMD `typed.TypedValue`, calls the SMD library's `merge.Updater.Update()` or `.Apply()`, then converts the result back |\n\nThe `Manager` interface itself is defined in `internal/manager.go`:\n\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\nNote that the inner signature carries `Managed` (the decoded field ownership map) separately from\nthe object, so the object stored in etcd never carries the managed fields during internal\nprocessing. `EncodeObjectManagedFields` / `RemoveObjectManagedFields` are used at the\n`FieldManager` boundary to translate between the wire format and the internal representation.\n\n### 2.4 structuredMergeManager and the SMD Library\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go`\n\nThis is the only layer that calls the external SMD library. It holds a `merge.Updater` configured\nwith:\n\n- A `Converter` \u2014 either `newVersionConverter` (for built-in types) or\n  `newCRDVersionConverter` (for CRDs) \u2014 which the SMD library calls to convert objects between API\n  versions during merge.\n- An `IgnoreFilter` \u2014 a `fieldpath.Filter` map (`resetFields`) specifying which fields to ignore\n  per API version (used to strip server-side defaults from managed-field tracking, e.g., for\n  `status` on create).\n\nFor an apply operation, `structuredMergeManager.Apply()`:\n1. Validates that the patch object's GVK matches `f.groupVersion`.\n2. Rejects patch objects that contain `metadata.managedFields` (clients must not submit managed fields).\n3. Converts both the patch object and the live object to `typed.TypedValue`.\n4. Calls `f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)`.\n5. Converts the result back: first to a versioned object, runs the defaulter, then converts to the hub (internal) version.\n\nThe SMD library returns `merge.Conflicts` if `force=false` and another manager owns a field in the\npatch. The `FieldManager.Apply()` method in `internal/fieldmanager.go` catches this and calls\n`NewConflictError()` to produce an HTTP 409 with structured `StatusCause` entries.\n\n### 2.5 TypeConverter\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/typeconverter.go`\n\n`TypeConverter` bridges Kubernetes objects and the SMD library:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\n`NewTypeConverter(openapiSpec, preserveUnknownFields)` builds a `typeConverter` by:\n1. Calling `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI` to produce the SMD schema.\n2. Iterating over the OpenAPI spec to extract `x-kubernetes-group-version-kind` extensions and\n   building a `map[schema.GroupVersionKind]*typed.ParseableType`.\n\n`ObjectToTyped` looks up the parser by GVK. If the GVK is not in the map, it returns a\n`NoCorrespondingTypeError`, which causes the merge to fall back to treating the object atomically.\n\nFor CRDs, `NewDeducedTypeConverter()` returns a `deducedTypeConverter` that calls\n`typed.DeducedParseableType.FromUnstructured()`; all lists are treated as atomic because there is\nno schema information to determine merge keys.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 HTTP Entry Point\n\nAll PATCH requests arrive at `PatchResource()` in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`:\n\n```go\nfunc PatchResource(r rest.Patcher, scope *RequestScope, admit admission.Interface, patchTypes []string) http.HandlerFunc\n```\n\nThe handler reads the `Content-Type` header and routes to different `patchMechanism`\nimplementations:\n\n| Content-Type | Mechanism |\n|---|---|\n| `application/json-patch+json` | `jsonPatcher` |\n| `application/merge-patch+json` | `jsonPatcher` |\n| `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` | `patcher` (strategic merge) |\n| `application/apply-patch+yaml` | `applyPatcher` |\n| `application/apply-patch+cbor` | `applyPatcher` (behind feature gate) |\n\nFor SSA, the `applyPatcher` struct is used:\n\n```go\n// patch.go:488\ntype applyPatcher struct {\n    patch               []byte\n    options             *metav1.PatchOptions\n    creater             runtime.ObjectCreater\n    kind                schema.GroupVersionKind\n    fieldManager        *managedfields.FieldManager\n    userAgent           string\n    validationDirective string\n    unmarshalFn         func(data []byte, v interface{}) error\n    unmarshalStrictFn   func(data []byte, v interface{}) error\n}\n```\n\n### 3.2 Apply Sequence\n\nThe `patcher.patchResource()` method calls the storage layer's `GuaranteedUpdate`, which\nin turn calls `p.applyPatch()` in a retry loop:\n\n```go\n// patch.go:578-620 (applyPatch)\nfunc (p *patcher) applyPatch(ctx context.Context, _, currentObject runtime.Object) (...) {\n    if !currentObjectHasUID {\n        // Object does not exist yet: create and apply\n        objToUpdate, patchErr = p.mechanism.createNewObject(ctx)\n    } else {\n        // Object exists: apply patch to current state\n        objToUpdate, patchErr = p.mechanism.applyPatchToCurrentObject(ctx, currentObject)\n    }\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n`applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject()` (patch.go:500):\n1. Deserialises the YAML/CBOR body into an `*unstructured.Unstructured`.\n2. Calls `p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)`.\n3. If `fieldValidation=Strict`, additionally validates the YAML with the strict decoder.\n\n`applyPatcher.createNewObject()` (patch.go:532):\n1. Creates an empty object with `p.creater.New(p.kind)`.\n2. Calls `applyPatchToCurrentObject` on the empty object \u2014 the SMD merge against an empty live\n   object is effectively a create.\n\n### 3.3 Inside FieldManager.Apply\n\n`internal/fieldmanager.go:183`:\n```go\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (object runtime.Object, err error) {\n    managed, err := DecodeManagedFields(accessor.GetManagedFields())  // decode from wire format\n    object, managed, err = f.fieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managed, manager, force)\n    if err != nil {\n        if conflicts, ok := err.(merge.Conflicts); ok {\n            return nil, NewConflictError(conflicts)  // convert to HTTP 409\n        }\n        return nil, err\n    }\n    if err = EncodeObjectManagedFields(object, managed); err != nil { ... }\n    return object, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe call traverses the decorator stack (see \u00a72.3.1), bottom to top:\n\n1. `structuredMergeManager.Apply()` performs the SMD merge, producing a new merged object and\n   updated `fieldpath.ManagedFields`.\n2. `StripMetaManager` removes system fields from the manager's field set.\n3. `ManagedFieldsUpdater` sets the timestamp on the manager's entry.\n4. `BuildManagerInfoManager` has already serialised the manager identifier before passing down.\n5. `CapManagersManager` (no-op for Apply, applies only on Update).\n6. `ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager` handles the bootstrap case.\n7. `LastAppliedManager` migrates annotation-based tracking if needed.\n8. `LastAppliedUpdater` syncs the kubectl annotation.\n9. `VersionCheckManager` validated the GVK before delegating.\n\n### 3.4 Inside structuredMergeManager.Apply\n\n`internal/structuredmerge.go:121`:\n\n```go\nfunc (f *structuredMergeManager) Apply(liveObj, patchObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error) {\n    // 1. Version check: patchObj GVK must match f.groupVersion\n    // 2. Reject patch objects with managedFields\n    liveObjVersioned, _ := f.toVersioned(liveObj)\n    patchObjTyped, _ := f.typeConverter.ObjectToTyped(patchObj)        // no AllowDuplicates: patch must be clean\n    liveObjTyped, _ := f.typeConverter.ObjectToTyped(liveObjVersioned, typed.AllowDuplicates)\n    apiVersion := fieldpath.APIVersion(f.groupVersion.String())\n\n    // 3. The SMD merge\n    newObjTyped, managedFields, err := f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)\n\n    // 4. Convert back: typed \u2192 unstructured \u2192 default \u2192 hub version\n    newObj, _ := f.typeConverter.TypedToObject(newObjTyped)\n    newObjVersioned, _ := f.toVersioned(newObj)\n    f.objectDefaulter.Default(newObjVersioned)\n    newObjUnversioned, _ := f.toUnversioned(newObjVersioned)\n    return newObjUnversioned, NewManaged(managedFields, managed.Times()), nil\n}\n```\n\nThe defaulter runs on the merged result so that server-filled defaults (e.g., `imagePullPolicy`)\nare present before the result is stored.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Conflict Handling\n\n### 4.1 What Constitutes a Conflict\n\nA conflict occurs when the applied configuration includes a field that is already owned by a\n**different** manager in the live object's managed fields. The SMD library's `merge.Updater.Apply`\nreturns a `merge.Conflicts` value (a slice of `{Manager, Path}` pairs) in this case.\n\n### 4.2 Conflict Error Representation\n\n`internal/conflict.go:33`:\n\n```go\nfunc NewConflictError(conflicts merge.Conflicts) *errors.StatusError {\n    causes := []metav1.StatusCause{}\n    for _, conflict := range conflicts {\n        causes = append(causes, metav1.StatusCause{\n            Type:    metav1.CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict,\n            Message: fmt.Sprintf(\"conflict with %v\", printManager(conflict.Manager)),\n            Field:   conflict.Path.String(),\n        })\n    }\n    return errors.NewApplyConflict(causes, getConflictMessage(conflicts))\n}\n```\n\nThe HTTP response is a 409 Conflict. Each `StatusCause` identifies the field path and the manager\nthat currently owns it.\n\n### 4.3 Resolution Patterns\n\n| Pattern | Mechanism | Trade-off |\n|---|---|---|\n| Force takeover | `Force: true` in `ApplyOptions` | Unconditionally reassigns ownership; appropriate for controllers that fully own their fields |\n| Remove the field | Omit the field from the next apply config | Relinquishes ownership; the field will be managed by whoever claimed it last |\n| Use a different fieldManager name | Change `FieldManager` string | Allows co-ownership under distinct manager identities |\n| Read-extract-modify-apply | Use `ExtractInto` to base the apply config on existing ownership | Avoids accidental ownership claims; suitable for legacy controller migration |\n\n### 4.4 Force-Apply Behaviour\n\nWhen `force=true`, the SMD library reassigns field ownership from the conflicting managers to the\ncaller without returning an error. The previous owner's field set is narrowed to exclude the\ncontested fields. If the previous owner's field set becomes empty, its entry is removed from\n`metadata.managedFields`.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Workflow Patterns\n\n### 5.1 Full-Reconciliation (Mechanism 1)\n\nSuitable for new controllers that own a well-defined set of fields:\n\n```go\n// pkg/controller/clusterroleaggregation/clusterroleaggregation_controller.go:143\nclusterRoleApply := rbacv1ac.ClusterRole(name).\n    WithRules(toApplyPolicyRules(newPolicyRules)...)\n\nopts := metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"clusterrole-aggregation-controller\", Force: true}\n_, err := c.clusterRoleClient.ClusterRoles().Apply(ctx, clusterRoleApply, opts)\n```\n\nThe controller reconstructs the full apply configuration on every reconciliation and sets\n`Force: true`. This guarantees idempotency and handles the case where a human or other controller\nhas modified a field the controller owns.\n\n### 5.2 Extract-Modify-Apply (Mechanism 2)\n\nSuitable for controllers with conditional code paths where not all fields are always set:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go:130\nfieldMgr := \"my-field-manager\"\ndeployment, _ := deploymentClient.Get(ctx, \"example-deployment\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n\n// Extract only the fields currently owned by this manager\ndeploymentAC, _ := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldMgr)\n\n// Modify in place\ndeploymentAC.Spec.Template.Spec.WithContainers(\n    corev1ac.Container().WithName(\"app\").WithImage(\"nginx:1.14.2\"),\n)\n\n// Apply; the resulting patch contains only the manager's owned fields plus modifications\napplied, _ := deploymentClient.Apply(ctx, deploymentAC, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: fieldMgr})\n```\n\n`ExtractDeployment` calls `managedfields.ExtractInto`:\n\n```go\n// managedfields/extract.go:53\nfunc ExtractInto(object runtime.Object, objectType typed.ParseableType, fieldManager string,\n                 applyConfiguration interface{}, subresource string) error {\n    typedObj, _ := toTyped(object, objectType)\n    fieldsEntry, ok := findManagedFields(accessor, fieldManager, subresource)\n    if !ok { return nil }  // no fields owned: leave applyConfiguration empty\n    fieldset := &fieldpath.Set{}\n    fieldset.FromJSON(bytes.NewReader(fieldsEntry.FieldsV1.Raw))\n    u := typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves()).AsValue().Unstructured()\n    runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter.FromUnstructured(u.(map[string]interface{}), applyConfiguration)\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\nKey details:\n- `ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` extracts only the *leaf* fields (not intermediate nodes). This\n  produces the minimal representation that the manager is entitled to reclaim.\n- The function must be called on the **root** resource object, not a subresource, because only root\n  objects carry their own managed fields.\n- If the manager has no managed fields yet (first invocation), the function returns without error\n  and `applyConfiguration` is left at its zero value.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Managed Fields Encoding\n\n### 6.1 Wire Format\n\n`metadata.managedFields` is a `[]metav1.ManagedFieldsEntry`. Each entry has:\n\n```go\ntype ManagedFieldsEntry struct {\n    Manager     string\n    Operation   ManagedFieldsOperationType  // \"Apply\" or \"Update\"\n    APIVersion  string\n    Time        *Time\n    FieldsType  string    // always \"FieldsV1\"\n    FieldsV1    *FieldsV1  // JSON-encoded fieldpath.Set\n    Subresource string\n}\n```\n\n### 6.2 Internal Format\n\nInternally, managed fields are a `fieldpath.ManagedFields` (a `map[string]fieldpath.VersionedSet`),\nwhere the key is a JSON-serialised manager identifier (produced by `BuildManagerIdentifier`).\n\nThe identifier includes manager name, operation, API version (for updates only), and subresource.\nFor **apply** operations, the APIVersion is excluded so the same applier retains a stable identity\nacross version upgrades:\n\n```go\n// internal/managedfields.go:148\nif encodedManager.Operation == metav1.ManagedFieldsOperationApply {\n    encodedManagerCopy.APIVersion = \"\"\n}\n```\n\nFor **update** operations, the API version is included, which means a controller that upgrades the\nAPI version it uses generates a new manager entry (old entry is merged into the bucket of the\nsame version or lost if the CapManagersManager threshold is reached).\n\n### 6.3 Decode/Encode Cycle\n\n`DecodeManagedFields()` reads from the wire format; `EncodeObjectManagedFields()` writes back.\nThe encode path sorts entries (by operation, time, manager name, API version, subresource) so that\ndiffs between stored objects are deterministic.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 7.1 Failure Modes\n\n| Failure | Behaviour |\n|---|---|\n| Patch YAML fails to deserialise | HTTP 400 Bad Request |\n| Patch GVK does not match resource GVK | HTTP 400 (caught by `VersionCheckManager`) |\n| Patch includes `metadata.managedFields` | HTTP 400 (caught by `structuredMergeManager`) |\n| Field conflict without `force=true` | HTTP 409 with `StatusCause` per conflicting field |\n| `TypeConverter` has no schema for the GVK | `NoCorrespondingTypeError`; falls back to atomic merge semantics |\n| `EncodeObjectManagedFields` fails | HTTP 500; managed fields are cleared from the returned object |\n| `UpdateNoErrors` path (used for regular updates) | On error, managed fields are cleared silently; logged at most once per second |\n\n### 7.2 Limits\n\n- **Max update managers:** 10 (`DefaultMaxUpdateManagers`). Exceeded entries are merged into\n  per-API-version `\"ancient-changes\"` buckets by `CapManagersManager`. This is a lossy operation:\n  once merged, individual manager history is gone.\n- **No limit on apply managers:** Apply managers are not capped, because each represents an active\n  intent owner. Objects with many SSA controllers accumulate proportionally.\n- **`metadata.managedFields` size:** Unbounded in practice; large numbers of apply managers or\n  field sets on large objects can inflate object size noticeably.\n\n### 7.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n**Pointer-for-all-fields** in applyconfigurations is the right design for expressing partial\nintent, but it makes the generated types incompatible with the normal API types. Controllers must\nmaintain parallel codepaths \u2014 one using the normal type for reads, one using the apply\nconfiguration for writes. The extract-modify-apply pattern bridges this.\n\n**CRD merge semantics:** CRDs use a deduced type converter that treats all lists as atomic, meaning\nSSA on CRD list fields replaces the entire list rather than merging by key. To get true list-merge\nsemantics, a CRD must provide an OpenAPI schema with `x-kubernetes-list-type: map` and\n`x-kubernetes-list-map-keys` annotations. Without a schema, the \"structured merge\" is structurally\natomic.\n\n**Probabilistic tracking on create:** `DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability` is 1.0, meaning all new\nobjects are tracked from creation. Setting it lower reduces overhead for objects never touched by\nSSA, but makes the first apply more expensive (the bootstrap path runs an `Update` to record\npre-existing fields).\n\n**kubectl annotation compatibility:** The `LastAppliedUpdater` syncs the\n`kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation only when the field manager is\n`\"kubectl\"`. Operators using a custom field manager name bypass this sync. This is intentional\n(opt-out by name) but means tools that depend on the annotation (some GitOps systems) may see stale\nvalues if a custom-named SSA controller is used.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Extension Points and Customisation Hooks\n\n### 8.1 Custom Field Managers\n\nThe `fieldManager` string in `ApplyOptions` is the primary extension point. Each unique value\ncreates an independent ownership domain. Conventions:\n\n- Controllers should use a stable, unique name (e.g., `\"clusterrole-aggregation-controller\"`).\n- kubectl uses `\"kubectl\"` for SSA and `\"kubectl-client-side-apply\"` for the annotation-based\n  approach (defined as `FieldManagerClientSideApply` and `fieldManagerServerSideApply` in\n  `staging/src/k8s.io/kubectl/pkg/cmd/apply/apply.go`).\n- Using `\"kubectl\"` as a custom controller's field manager triggers the annotation-sync logic in\n  `LastAppliedUpdater`, which is unlikely to be desired.\n\n### 8.2 resetFields (IgnoreFilter)\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` accept a\n`map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` parameter called `resetFields`. This filter is passed\nto the SMD library's `merge.Updater.IgnoreFilter` and tells the merger to strip certain fields from\nfield ownership tracking \u2014 for example, `status` on create (since status is server-filled).\n\nResources that want to prevent certain fields from being owned by any manager wire this up when\nthey install the FieldManager. There is no hook for controllers to provide custom `resetFields`;\nthis is configured by the API server at resource registration time.\n\n### 8.3 External Apply Configurations\n\nThe `applyconfiguration-gen` tool accepts `--external-applyconfigurations` (defined in\n`args/args.go`) to reuse existing generated apply configurations for types from other packages. The\ndefault includes:\n\n```go\n{Package: \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\", Name: \"Condition\"}: \"k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1\"\n```\n\nProjects that generate their own apply configurations for CRD types use this mechanism to point the\ngenerator at the right package for shared types.\n\n### 8.4 CEL-Based Apply Configuration in Mutating Admission Policies\n\nA newer extension point: `MutatingAdmissionPolicy` (alpha) supports a `PatchTypeApplyConfiguration`\nmutation type. The admission plugin compiles a CEL expression that returns an apply configuration\nobject, then calls `ApplyStructuredMergeDiff()` in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/policy/mutating/patch/smd.go` to apply it.\nThis uses the same `managedfields` machinery but invokes it inside the admission chain rather than\nat the storage layer.\n\n### 8.5 ScaleHandler for Subresource Mapping\n\n`managedfields.NewScaleHandler` is the hook used by resources that expose a `scale` subresource.\nIt translates field paths between the main resource schema and the `autoscaling/v1.Scale` schema.\nResources that need this wire it in their REST handler. It is not extensible from outside the\nKubernetes codebase without forking.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 Performance\n\n**Apply is more expensive than Update.** An apply involves:\n1. Deserialising the entire live object from storage.\n2. Converting both the live and patch objects to `typed.TypedValue` (involves OpenAPI schema\n   lookup and typed traversal).\n3. Running the SMD merge algorithm (graph traversal over the field tree).\n4. Re-defaulting the merged object.\n5. Serialising the managed fields and storing the result.\n\nRegular updates only need step 5 (plus the storage round-trip). For high-frequency writes on large\nobjects (e.g., node status updates), the SSA path has measurable overhead; status subresource\nupdates remain as regular `Update` operations for this reason.\n\n**TypeConverter is a hot path.** The `typeConverter.parser` map is built once at startup from the\nOpenAPI spec and is read-only during serving. No lock is needed for reads. For CRDs with a schema,\nthe CRD handler refreshes the type converter on schema changes.\n\n### 9.2 managedFields Bloat\n\n`metadata.managedFields` grows with the number of distinct managers and API versions. Contributors\nto field bloat:\n\n- Many SSA controllers on the same object.\n- API version upgrades: update managers carry the version in their identity, so upgrading from\n  `apps/v1beta1` to `apps/v1` adds new entries. Old entries are eventually merged into\n  `\"ancient-changes\"` if the 10-entry cap is reached.\n- Large field sets on objects with many fields (e.g., Nodes).\n\nThe `CapManagersManager` provides a hard limit for update managers but not for apply managers.\nOperators should avoid giving each reconciliation loop a unique field manager name (e.g., do not\ninclude a pod name in the field manager string).\n\n### 9.3 Reliability and Conflict Avoidance\n\nSSA makes multi-controller collaboration explicit and reliable, but requires coordination:\n\n- **Controllers must use `Force: true`** if they are the authoritative owner of a field.\n  Not using `Force` means a stale field set (from a previous manager) can block the controller's\n  apply and cause continuous reconciliation errors.\n- **Removing fields from an apply config** implicitly relinquishes ownership. If a controller\n  conditionally omits a field, and another manager claims it, the original controller can no longer\n  set that field without a conflict or force.\n- **Admission webhooks** that mutate objects during apply are opaque to managed fields: mutations\n  performed by webhooks are attributed to the original applier's field manager, which can cause\n  surprising ownership. The `MutatingAdmissionPolicy` CEL approach is the structured alternative.\n\n### 9.4 Maintainability\n\n**Generated code must be regenerated** whenever an API type changes. The `Makefile` target\n`generate` runs `applyconfiguration-gen`. Failing to regenerate causes compile errors in the typed\nclient, since the `Apply()` method signature references the apply configuration type.\n\nThe separation between the `applyconfigurations` package (generated, all-pointer structs) and the\nAPI types (generated, mixed value/pointer structs) means there are two type systems in parallel.\nThis is a known maintenance cost accepted in exchange for correctness.\n\n---\n\n## 10. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Generated client-side apply configuration types, one subdirectory per API group/version |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go` | Package-level documentation; explains the pointer-based design and both controller patterns |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/utils.go` | Generated `ForKind(gvk)` helper; type-lookup by GVK |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go` | Public `FieldManager` type and constructors (`NewDefaultFieldManager`, `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager`) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go` | `ExtractInto()` \u2014 the extract half of the extract-modify-apply pattern |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/scalehandler.go` | `ScaleHandler` \u2014 path mapping for scale subresource |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/typeconverter.go` | Public `TypeConverter` interface and `NewTypeConverter()` factory |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/manager.go` | `Manager` interface definition |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go` | `FieldManager` struct; `Apply()` and `Update()` entry points; conflict error translation; `NewDefaultFieldManager` stack assembly |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go` | `structuredMergeManager`; calls SMD library `merge.Updater` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/managedfields.go` | Wire format encode/decode; `BuildManagerIdentifier`; `DecodeManagedFields`; routes to `applyPatcher` for SSA; calls `FieldManager.Apply` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/` | `applyconfiguration-gen` tool source |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/generators/targets.go` | Generator entry point;
